</tr>

<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:War" title="Template:War"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:War" title="Template talk:War"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:War&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>War</b> is a state of armed conflict between <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">societies</a>. It is generally characterized by extreme <a href="/wiki/Aggression" title="Aggression">aggression</a>, destruction, and mortality, using <a href="/wiki/Regular_army" title="Regular army">regular</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irregular_military" title="Irregular military">irregular</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Military forces">military forces</a>. An absence of war is usually called "<a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a>". <b>Warfare</b> refers to the common activities and characteristics of types of war, or of wars in general.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">Total war</a> is warfare that is not restricted to purely <a href="/wiki/Legitimate_military_target" title="Legitimate military target">legitimate military targets</a>, and can result in massive <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualties" title="Civilian casualties">civilian</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Non-combatant" title="Non-combatant">non-combatant</a> <a href="/wiki/Casualties" class="mw-redirect" title="Casualties">casualties</a>.</p>
<p>While some scholars see war as a universal and ancestral aspect of <a href="/wiki/Human_nature" title="Human nature">human nature</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> others argue it is a result of specific socio-cultural or ecological circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-Sage_Publications_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sage_Publications-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The deadliest war in history, in terms of the cumulative number of deaths since its start, is the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, from 1939 to 1945, with 60–85 million deaths, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquests" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol conquests">Mongol conquests</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> which was greater than 41 million. As concerns a belligerent's losses in proportion to its prewar population, the most destructive war in <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">modern history</a> may have been the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War_casualties" title="Paraguayan War casualties">Paraguayan War casualties</a>). In 2013 war resulted in 31,000 deaths, down from 72,000 deaths in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-GDB2013_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDB2013-5">[5]</a></sup> In 2003, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Smalley" title="Richard Smalley">Richard Smalley</a> identified war as the sixth (of ten) biggest problem facing <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humanity</a> for the next fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> War usually results in significant deterioration of infrastructure and the ecosystem, a decrease in social spending, <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>, large-scale emigration from the war zone, and often the mistreatment of <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> or <a href="/wiki/Civilians" class="mw-redirect" title="Civilians">civilians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> For instance, of the nine million people who were on the territory of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Belarus" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Belarus">Soviet Belarus</a> in 1941, some 1.6 million were killed by the Germans in actions away from battlefields, including about 700,000 prisoners of war, 500,000 Jews, and 320,000 people counted as partisans (the vast majority of whom were unarmed civilians).<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Another byproduct of some wars is the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a> by some or all parties in the conflict,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and increased revenues by <a href="/wiki/Weapons_manufacturers" class="mw-redirect" title="Weapons manufacturers">weapons manufacturers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg/350px-Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg" width="350" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg/525px-Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg/700px-Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="5436" data-file-height="1865" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mural of War (1896), by <a href="/wiki/Gari_Melchers" title="Gari Melchers">Gari Melchers</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The English word <i>war</i> derives from the late <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> (circa.1050) words <i>wyrre</i> and <i>werre</i>, from <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> <i>werre</i> (also <i>guerre</i> as in modern French), in turn from the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> *<i>werra</i>, ultimately deriving from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a> *<i>werzō</i> 'mixture, confusion'. The word is related to the <a href="/wiki/Old_Saxon" title="Old Saxon">Old Saxon</a> <i>werran</i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> <i>werran</i>, and the German <i>verwirren</i>, meaning “to confuse”, “to perplex”, and “to bring into confusion”.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In German, the equivalent is <i>Krieg</i> (from Proto-Germanic *<i>krīganą</i> 'to strive, be stubborn'); the Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, and Italian term for "war" is <i>guerra</i>, derived like the Old French term from the Germanic word.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Etymologic legend has it that the Romanic peoples adopted a foreign, Germanic word for "war", to avoid using the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>bellum</i>, because, when sounded, it tended to merge with the sound of the word <i>bello</i> ("beautiful").<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/War_studies" title="War studies">scholarly study of war</a> is sometimes called polemology (<a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>: <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/dʒ/ 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>pah-lə-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">MAHL</span></span></b>-ə-jee</i></a></span>), from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>polemos</i>, meaning "war", and <i><a href="/wiki/-logy" title="-logy">-logy</a></i>, meaning "the study of".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_war#Types_of_war" title="Outline of war">Types of war</a></div>
<p>War must entail some degree of confrontation using weapons and other <a href="/wiki/Military_technology_and_equipment" class="mw-redirect" title="Military technology and equipment">military technology and equipment</a> by armed forces employing <a href="/wiki/Military_tactics" title="Military tactics">military tactics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operational_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Operational art">operational art</a> within a broad <a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">military strategy</a> subject to <a href="/wiki/Military_logistics" title="Military logistics">military logistics</a>. Studies of war by military theorists throughout <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">military history</a> have sought to identify the <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_war" title="Philosophy of war">philosophy of war</a>, and to reduce it to a <a href="/wiki/Military_science" title="Military science">military science</a>. Modern military science considers several factors before a <a href="/wiki/Defence_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Defence policy">national defence policy</a> is created to allow a war to commence: the environment in the area(s) of combat operations, the posture national forces will adopt on the commencement of a war, and the type of warfare troops will be engaged in.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_warfare" title="Asymmetric warfare">Asymmetric warfare</a></b> is a conflict between two populations of drastically different levels of military capability or size.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">Biological warfare</a></b>, or germ warfare, is the use of weaponized biological toxins or infectious agents such as bacteria, viruses, and fungi.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">Chemical warfare</a></b> involves the use of weaponized chemicals in combat. Poison gas as a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">chemical weapon</a> was principally used during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and resulted in over a million estimated casualties, including more than 100,000 civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224,_Guernica,_Ruinen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="593" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224,_Guernica,_Ruinen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of <a href="/wiki/Guernica" title="Guernica">Guernica</a> (1937). The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> was one of Europe's bloodiest and most brutal civil wars.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">Civil war</a></b> is a war between forces belonging to the same nation or political entity.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Conventional_warfare" title="Conventional warfare">Conventional warfare</a></b> is declared war between states in which <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biological_weapon" class="mw-redirect" title="Biological weapon">biological</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical weapons">chemical weapons</a> are not used or see limited deployment.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">Cyberwarfare</a></b> involves the actions by a nation-state or international organization to attack and attempt to damage another nation's information systems.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Information_warfare" title="Information warfare">Information warfare</a></b> is the application of destructive force on a large scale against information assets and systems, against the <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Network" class="mw-disambig" title="Network">networks</a> that support the four critical infrastructures (the power grid, communications, financial, and transportation).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">Nuclear warfare</a></b> is warfare in which <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> are the primary, or a major, method of achieving capitulation.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">Total war</a></b> is warfare by any means possible, disregarding the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of war">laws of war</a>, placing no limits on <a href="/wiki/Legitimate_military_target" title="Legitimate military target">legitimate military targets</a>, using <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">weapons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_tactics" title="Military tactics">tactics</a> resulting in significant <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualties" title="Civilian casualties">civilian casualties</a>, or demanding a <a href="/wiki/War_effort" title="War effort">war effort</a> requiring significant sacrifices by the friendly civilian population.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Unconventional_warfare" title="Unconventional warfare">Unconventional warfare</a></b>, the opposite of conventional warfare, is an attempt to achieve military victory through acquiescence, capitulation, or clandestine support for one side of an existing conflict.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/War_of_aggression" title="War of aggression">War of aggression</a></b> is a war for conquest or gain rather than self-defense; this can be the basis of <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> under <a href="/wiki/Customary_international_law" title="Customary international law">customary international law</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">Military history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg/310px-War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg.png" width="310" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg/465px-War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg/620px-War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1191" data-file-height="842" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The percentages of men killed in war in eight tribal societies, and Europe and the U.S. in the 20th century. (Lawrence H. Keeley, Archeologist)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The earliest recorded evidence of war belongs to the Mesolithic cemetery <a href="/wiki/Site_117" class="mw-redirect" title="Site 117">Site 117</a>, which has been determined to be approximately 14,000 years old. About forty-five percent of the skeletons there displayed signs of violent death.<sup id="cite_ref-Keeley_page_37_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keeley_page_37-17">[17]</a></sup> Since the rise of the <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> some 5,000 years ago,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> military activity has occurred over much of the globe. The advent of <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a> and the acceleration of technological advances led to modern warfare. According to Conway W. Henderson, <i>"One source claims that 14,500 wars have taken place between 3500 BC and the late 20th century, costing 3.5 billion lives, leaving only 300 years of peace (Beer 1981: 20)."</i><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> An unfavorable review of this estimate<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> mentions the following regarding one of the proponents of this estimate: <i>«In addition, perhaps feeling that the war casualties figure was improbably high, he changed "approximately 3,640,000,000 human beings have been killed by war or the diseases produced by war" to "approximately 1,240,000,000 human beings...&amp;c.".»</i> The lower figure is more plausible,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> but could also be on the high side, considering that the 100 deadliest acts of mass violence between 480 BCE and 2002 CE (wars and other man-made disasters with at least 300,000 and up to 66 million victims) claimed about 455 million human lives in total.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Primitive warfare is estimated to have accounted for 15.1&#160;% of deaths and claimed 400 million victims.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Added to the aforementioned (and perhaps too high) figure of 1,240 million between 3500 BC and the late 20th century, this would mean a total of 1,640,000,000 people killed by war (including deaths from famine and disease caused by war) throughout the history and pre-history of mankind. For comparison, an estimated 1,680,000,000 people died from infectious diseases in the 20th Century.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">Nuclear warfare</a> breaking out in August 1988, when nuclear arsenals were at peak level, and the aftermath thereof, could have reduced human population from 5,150,000,000 by 1,850,000,000 to 3,300,000,000 within a period of about one year, according to a projection that doesn't consider "the most severe predictions concerning <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_winter" title="Nuclear winter">nuclear winter</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> This would have been a proportional reduction of the world’s population exceeding the reduction caused in the 14th Century by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, and comparable in proportional terms with the plague’s impact on Europe's population in 1346–53.</p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/War_Before_Civilization" title="War Before Civilization">War Before Civilization</a></i>, Lawrence H. Keeley, a professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" title="University of Illinois at Urbana–Champaign">University of Illinois</a>, says approximately 90–95% of known societies throughout history engaged in at least occasional warfare,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and many fought constantly.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Keeley describes several styles of primitive combat such as small raids, large raids, and massacres. All of these forms of warfare were used by primitive societies, a finding supported by other researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Keeley explains that early war raids were not well organized, as the participants did not have any formal training. Scarcity of resources meant defensive works were not a cost effective way to protect the society against enemy raids.<sup id="cite_ref-Keeley_page_55_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keeley_page_55-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_Rubinstein" title="William Rubinstein">William Rubinstein</a> wrote "Pre-literate societies, even those organised in a relatively advanced way, were renowned for their studied cruelty...'archaeology yields evidence of prehistoric massacres more severe than any recounted in ethnography [i.e., after the coming of the Europeans].'"<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg/240px-MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg" width="240" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg/360px-MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg/480px-MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1597" data-file-height="740" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Japanese <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a> attacking a <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol</a> ship, 13th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Western Europe, since the late 18th century, more than 150 conflicts and about 600 battles have taken place.<sup id="cite_ref-War_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-War-31">[31]</a></sup> During the 20th century, war resulted in a dramatic intensification of the pace of social changes, and was a crucial catalyst for the emergence of the Left as a force to be reckoned with.<sup id="cite_ref-Kolko_1994_xviitoxviii_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kolko_1994_xviitoxviii-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recent rapid increases in the technologies of war, and therefore in its destructiveness (see <a href="/wiki/Mutual_assured_destruction" title="Mutual assured destruction">mutual assured destruction</a>), have caused widespread public concern, and have in all probability forestalled, and may altogether prevent the outbreak of a nuclear World War III. At the end of each of the last two World Wars, concerted and popular efforts were made to come to a greater understanding of the underlying dynamics of war and to thereby hopefully reduce or even eliminate it altogether. These efforts materialized in the forms of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, and its successor, the United Nations.</p>
<p>Shortly after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, as a token of support for this concept, most nations joined the United Nations. During this same post-war period, with the aim of further delegitimizing war as an acceptable and logical extension of foreign policy<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, most national governments also renamed their Ministries or Departments of War as their Ministries or Departments of Defense, for example, the former U.S. Department of War was renamed as the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Defense" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn,_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn%2C_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg/220px-Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn%2C_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn%2C_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg/330px-Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn%2C_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn%2C_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg/440px-Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn%2C_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1449" data-file-height="996" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Custer_Massacre_At_Big_Horn,_Montana_June_25_1876.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
According to the U.S. Bureau of the Census (1894), the <a href="/wiki/American_Indian_Wars" title="American Indian Wars">Indian Wars</a> of the 19th century cost the lives of about 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1947, in view of the rapidly increasingly destructive consequences of modern warfare, and with a particular concern for the consequences and costs of the newly developed <a href="/wiki/Atom_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atom bomb">atom bomb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> famously stated, "I know not with what weapons World War III will be fought, but World War IV will be fought with sticks and stones."<sup id="cite_ref-EinsteinWWIV_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EinsteinWWIV-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> urged the socialist camp not to fear nuclear war with the United States since, even if "half of mankind died, the other half would remain while imperialism would be razed to the ground and the whole world would become socialist."<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Human_Security_Report_2005" title="Human Security Report 2005">Human Security Report 2005</a> documented a significant decline in the number and severity of armed conflicts since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in the early 1990s. However, the evidence examined in the 2008 edition of the Center for International Development and Conflict Management's "Peace and Conflict" study indicated the overall decline in conflicts had stalled.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_by_death_toll">Largest by death toll</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll" title="List of wars by death toll">List of wars by death toll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_war#Wars" title="Outline of war">Outline of war §&#160;Wars</a></div>
<p>Three of the ten most costly wars, in terms of loss of life, have been waged in the last century. These are the two World Wars, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (which is sometimes considered part of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, or as overlapping). Most of the others involved China or neighboring peoples. The death toll of World War II, being over 60 million, surpasses all other war-death-tolls.<sup id="cite_ref-users.erols_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-users.erols-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
